talk:Astrodynamics"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Astrodynamics&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Orbital mechanics</b> or <b>space aerodynamics</b> is the application of <a href="/wiki/Ballistics" title="Ballistics">ballistics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Celestial_mechanics" title="Celestial mechanics">celestial mechanics</a> to the practical problems concerning the motion of <a href="/wiki/Rocket" title="Rocket">rockets</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">spacecraft</a>. The motion of these objects is usually calculated from <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_laws_of_motion" title="Newton\'s laws of motion">Newton\'s laws of motion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_law_of_universal_gravitation" title="Newton\'s law of universal gravitation">law of universal gravitation</a>. It is a core discipline within <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">space-mission</a> design and control.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Celestial_mechanics" title="Celestial mechanics">Celestial mechanics</a> treats more broadly the <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">orbital</a> dynamics of systems under the influence of <a href="/wiki/Gravity" title="Gravity">gravity</a>, including both spacecraft and natural <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_object" title="Astronomical object">astronomical bodies</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Star_system" title="Star system">star systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">moons</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Comet" title="Comet">comets</a>. Orbital mechanics focuses on spacecraft <a href="/wiki/Trajectory" title="Trajectory">trajectories</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Orbital_maneuver" title="Orbital maneuver">orbital maneuvers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orbital_plane_(astronomy)" title="Orbital plane (astronomy)">orbital plane</a> changes, and interplanetary transfers, and is used by mission planners to predict the results of <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft_propulsion" title="Spacecraft propulsion">propulsive maneuvers</a>. <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">General relativity</a> is a more exact theory than Newton\'s laws for calculating orbits, and is sometimes necessary for greater accuracy or in high-gravity situations (e.g. orbits near the Sun).\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orbital_mechanics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" decoding="async" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Orbital_mechanics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">August 2008</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Until the rise of <a href="/wiki/Spaceflight" title="Spaceflight">space travel</a> in the twentieth century, there was little distinction between orbital and celestial mechanics. At the time of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sputnik" title="Sputnik">Sputnik</a>, the field was termed \'space dynamics\'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The fundamental techniques, such as those used to solve the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keplerian_problem" title="Keplerian problem">Keplerian problem</a> (determining position as a function of time), are therefore the same in both fields. Furthermore, the history of the fields are almost entirely shared.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Johannes_Kepler" title="Johannes Kepler">Johannes Kepler</a> was the first to successfully model planetary orbits to a high degree of accuracy, publishing <a href="/wiki/Kepler%27s_laws_of_planetary_motion" title="Kepler\'s laws of planetary motion">his laws</a> in 1605. <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a> published more general laws of celestial motion in the first edition of <i><a href="/wiki/Philosophi%C3%A6_Naturalis_Principia_Mathematica" title="Philosophi&#230; Naturalis Principia Mathematica">Philosophi&#230; Naturalis Principia Mathematica</a></i> (1687), which gave a method for finding the orbit of a body following a <a href="/wiki/Parabola" title="Parabola">parabolic</a> path from three observations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> This was used by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edmund_Halley" title="Edmund Halley">Edmund Halley</a> to establish the orbits of various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comets" title="Comets">comets</a>, including that which bears his name. Newton\'s method of successive approximation was formalised into an analytic method by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euler" title="Euler">Euler</a> in 1744, whose work was in turn generalised to elliptical and hyperbolic orbits by <a href="/wiki/Johann_Heinrich_Lambert" title="Johann Heinrich Lambert">Lambert</a> in 1761-1777.\n</p><p>Another milestone in orbit determination was <a href="/wiki/Carl_Friedrich_Gauss" title="Carl Friedrich Gauss">Carl Friedrich Gauss</a>\'s assistance in the "recovery" of the <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet" title="Dwarf planet">dwarf planet</a> <a href="/wiki/Ceres_(dwarf_planet)" title="Ceres (dwarf planet)">Ceres</a> in 1801.  <a href="/wiki/Gauss%27s_method" title="Gauss\'s method">Gauss\'s method</a> was able to use just three observations (in the form of pairs of <a href="/wiki/Right_ascension" title="Right ascension">right ascension</a> and <a href="/wiki/Declination" title="Declination">declination</a>), to find the six <a href="/wiki/Orbital_elements" title="Orbital elements">orbital elements</a> that completely describe an orbit.  The theory of orbit determination has subsequently been developed to the point where today it is applied in GPS receivers as well as the tracking and cataloguing of newly observed <a href="/wiki/Minor_planet" title="Minor planet">minor planets</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Practical_techniques">Practical techniques</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orbital_mechanics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Practical techniques">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_orbits" title="List of orbits">List of orbits</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rules_of_thumb">Rules of thumb</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orbital_mechanics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Rules of thumb">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following rules of thumb are useful for situations approximated by <a href="/wiki/Classical_mechanics" title="Classical mechanics">classical mechanics</a> under the standard assumptions of astrodynamics outlined below the rules.  The specific example discussed is of a satellite orbiting a planet, but the rules of thumb could also apply to other situations, such as orbits of small bodies around a star such as the Sun.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kepler%27s_laws_of_planetary_motion" title="Kepler\'s laws of planetary motion">Kepler\'s laws of planetary motion</a>:\n<ul><li>Orbits are <a href="/wiki/Ellipse" title="Ellipse">elliptical</a>, with the heavier body at one <a href="/wiki/Focus_(geometry)" title="Focus (geometry)">focus</a> of the ellipse. Special case of this is a circular orbit (a circle is a special case of ellipse) with the planet at the center.</li>\n<li>A line drawn from the planet to the satellite sweeps out <i>equal areas in equal times</i> no matter which portion of the orbit is measured.</li>\n<li>The square of a satellite\'s orbital period is proportional to the cube of its average distance from the planet.</li></ul></li>\n<li>Without applying <a href="/wiki/Force" title="Force">force</a> (such as firing a rocket engine), the period and shape of the satellite\'s orbit won\'t change.</li>\n<li>A satellite in a low orbit (or low part of an elliptical orbit) moves more quickly with respect to the surface of the planet than a satellite in a higher orbit (or a high part of an elliptical orbit), due to the stronger gravitational attraction closer to the planet.</li>\n<li>If thrust is applied at only one point in the satellite\'s orbit, it will return to that same point on each subsequent orbit, though the rest of its path will change.  Thus one cannot move from one circular orbit to another with only one brief application of thrust.</li>\n<li>From a circular orbit, thrust applied in a direction opposite to the satellite\'s motion changes orbit to elliptical; the satellite will descend and reach the lowest orbital point (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Periapse" title="Periapse">periapse</a>) at 180 degrees away from the firing point; then it will ascend back. Thrust applied in the direction of the satellite\'s motion creates an elliptical orbit with its highest point (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apoapse" title="Apoapse">apoapse</a>) 180 degrees away from the firing point.</li></ul>\n<p>The consequences of the rules of orbital mechanics are sometimes counter-intuitive.  For example, if two spacecraft are in the same circular orbit and wish to dock, unless they are very close, the trailing craft cannot simply fire its engines to go faster.  This will change the shape of its orbit, causing it to gain altitude and actually slow down relative to the leading craft, missing the target. The <a href="/wiki/Space_rendezvous" title="Space rendezvous">space rendezvous</a> before docking normally takes multiple precisely calculated engine firings in multiple orbital periods requiring hours or even days to complete.\n</p><p>To the degree that the standard assumptions of astrodynamics do not hold, actual trajectories will vary from those calculated.  For example, simple <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atmospheric_drag" title="Atmospheric drag">atmospheric drag</a> is another complicating factor for objects in low <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth_orbit" title="Earth orbit">Earth orbit</a>.  These rules of thumb are decidedly inaccurate when describing two or more bodies of similar mass, such as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Binary_star_system" title="Binary star system">binary star system</a> (see <a href="/wiki/N-body_problem" title="N-body problem">n-body problem</a>). <a href="/wiki/Celestial_mechanics" title="Celestial mechanics">Celestial mechanics</a> uses more general rules applicable to a wider variety of situations. Kepler\'s laws of planetary motion, which can be mathematically derived from Newton\'s laws, hold strictly only in describing the motion of two gravitating bodies in the absence of non-gravitational forces; they also describe parabolic and hyperbolic trajectories. In the close proximity of large objects like stars the differences between <a href="/wiki/Classical_mechanics" title="Classical mechanics">classical mechanics</a> and <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a> also become important.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Laws_of_astrodynamics">Laws of astrodynamics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orbital_mechanics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Laws of astrodynamics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Laplace%E2%80%93Runge%E2%80%93Lenz_vector" title="Laplace&#8211;Runge&#8211;Lenz vector">Laplace&#8211;Runge&#8211;Lenz vector</a></div>\n<p>The fundamental laws of astrodynamics are <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_law_of_universal_gravitation" title="Newton\'s law of universal gravitation">Newton\'s law of universal gravitation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_laws_of_motion" title="Newton\'s laws of motion">Newton\'s laws of motion</a>, while the fundamental mathematical tool is his differential <a href="/wiki/Calculus" title="Calculus">calculus</a>.\n</p><p>Every orbit and trajectory outside atmospheres is in principle reversible, i.e., in the space-time function the time is reversed. The velocities are reversed and the accelerations are the same, including those due to rocket bursts. Thus if a rocket burst is in the direction of the velocity, in the reversed case it is opposite to the velocity. Of course in the case of rocket bursts there is no full reversal of events, both ways the same delta-v is used and the same <a href="/wiki/Mass_ratio" title="Mass ratio">mass ratio</a> applies.\n</p><p>Standard assumptions in astrodynamics include non-interference from outside bodies, negligible mass for one of the bodies, and negligible other forces (such as from the solar wind, atmospheric drag, etc.).  More accurate calculations can be made without these simplifying assumptions, but they are more complicated.  The increased accuracy often does not make enough of a difference in the calculation to be worthwhile.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Kepler%27s_laws_of_planetary_motion" title="Kepler\'s laws of planetary motion">Kepler\'s laws of planetary motion</a> may be derived from Newton\'s laws, when it is assumed that the orbiting body is subject only to the gravitational force of the central attractor. When an engine thrust or propulsive force is present, Newton\'s laws still apply, but Kepler\'s laws are invalidated.  When the thrust stops, the resulting orbit will be different but will once again be described by Kepler\'s laws.  The three laws are:\n</p>\n<ol><li>The <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">orbit</a> of every <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">planet</a> is an <a href="/wiki/Ellipse" title="Ellipse">ellipse</a> with the sun at one of the <a href="/wiki/Focus_(geometry)" title="Focus (geometry)">foci</a>.</li>\n<li>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Line_(mathematics)" title="Line (mathematics)">line</a> joining a planet and the sun sweeps out equal areas during equal intervals of time.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Square_(algebra)" title="Square (algebra)">squares</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Orbital_period" title="Orbital period">orbital periods</a> of planets are directly <a href="/wiki/Proportionality_(mathematics)" title="Proportionality (mathematics)">proportional</a> to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cube_(arithmetic)" title="Cube (arithmetic)">cubes</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-major_axis" title="Semi-major axis">semi-major axis</a> of the orbits.</li></ol>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Escape_velocity">Escape velocity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orbital_mechanics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Escape velocity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Escape_velocity" title="Escape velocity">Escape velocity</a></div>\n<p>The formula for an <a href="/wiki/Escape_velocity" title="Escape velocity">escape velocity</a> is easily derived as follows.  The <a href="/wiki/Specific_energy" title="Specific energy">specific energy</a> (energy per unit <a href="/wiki/Mass" title="Mass">mass</a>) of any space vehicle is composed of two components, the specific <a href="/wiki/Potential_energy" title="Potential energy">potential energy</a> and the specific <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">kinetic energy</a>. The specific potential energy associated with a planet of <a href="/wiki/Mass" title="Mass">mass</a> <i>M</i> is given by\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\epsilon _{p}=-{\\frac {GM}{r}}\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; width:12.402ex; height:5.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>while the <a href="/wiki/Specific_kinetic_energy" title="Specific kinetic energy">specific kinetic energy</a> of an object is given by\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\epsilon _{k}={\\frac {v^{2}}{2}}\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; width:8.536ex; height:5.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Since <a href="/wiki/Conservation_of_energy" title="Conservation of energy">energy is conserved</a>,\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\epsilon =\\epsilon _{k}+\\epsilon _{p},\\!}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; margin-right: -0.229ex; width:11.408ex; height:2.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>and so the total <a href="/wiki/Specific_orbital_energy" title="Specific orbital energy">specific orbital energy</a>\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\epsilon ={\\frac {v^{2}}{2}}-{\\frac {GM}{r}}\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; width:15.393ex; height:5.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>does not depend on the distance, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle r}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0d1ecb613aa2984f0576f70f86650b7c2a132538" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.049ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>, from the center of the central body to the space vehicle in question. Therefore, the object can reach infinite <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle r}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0d1ecb613aa2984f0576f70f86650b7c2a132538" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.049ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> only if this quantity is nonnegative, which implies\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v\\geq {\\sqrt {\\frac {2GM}{r}}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo>&#8805;<!-- &#8805; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>G</mi>\n<mi>M</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v\\geq {\\sqrt {\\frac {2GM}{r}}}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle v\\geq {\\sqrt {\\frac {2GM}{r}}}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/51957d7cceb3906a1a858dd4f77810771ff7014d" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:13.464ex; height:6.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>The escape velocity from the Earth\'s surface is about 11&#160;km/s, but that is insufficient to send the body an infinite distance because of the gravitational pull of the Sun. To escape the Solar System from a location at a distance from the Sun equal to the distance Sun&#8211;Earth, but not close to the Earth, requires around 42&#160;km/s velocity, but there will be "part credit" for the Earth\'s orbital velocity for spacecraft launched from Earth, if their further acceleration (due to the propulsion system) carries them in the same direction as Earth travels in its orbit.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formulae_for_free_orbits">Formulae for free orbits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orbital_mechanics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Formulae for free orbits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Orbits are <a href="/wiki/Conic_section" title="Conic section">conic sections</a>, so the formula for the distance of a body for a given angle corresponds to the formula for that curve in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polar_coordinates" title="Polar coordinates">polar coordinates</a>, which is:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle r={\\frac {p}{1+e\\cos \\theta }}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mrow>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mi>cos</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r={\\frac {p}{1+e\\cos \\theta }}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r = \\frac{ p }{1 + e \\cos \\theta}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e34b3d588b04110d81d435e06b36e023683a9a09" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:15.045ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mu =G(m_{1}+m_{2})\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>G</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mu =G(m_{1}+m_{2})\\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\mu= G(m_1+m_2)\\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/30d000d9d7592fc22fd4a07fd8440f8d07fe5433" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:17.553ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle p=h^{2}/\\mu \\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>h</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle p=h^{2}/\\mu \\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="p=h^2/\\mu\\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/60e212d6386cc2cf31869b40144b141f558c0800" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:9.702ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mu }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mu }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\mu " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9fd47b2a39f7a7856952afec1f1db72c67af6161" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:1.402ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is called the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gravitational_parameter" title="Gravitational parameter">gravitational parameter</a>. <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle m_{1}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle m_{1}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="m_{1}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/31aafa60e48d39ccce922404c0b80340b2cc777a" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.095ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle m_{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle m_{2}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="m_{2}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0ecebe334d5cadc3ffcf245eb02919034d7a2ec8" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:3.095ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> are the masses of objects 1 and 2, and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle h}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>h</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle h}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="h" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b26be3e694314bc90c3215047e4a2010c6ee184a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.339ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specific_angular_momentum" title="Specific angular momentum">specific angular momentum</a> of object 2 with respect to object 1. The parameter <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\theta }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\theta }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\theta " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6e5ab2664b422d53eb0c7df3b87e1360d75ad9af" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.09ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is known as the <a href="/wiki/True_anomaly" title="True anomaly">true anomaly</a>, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle p}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>p</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle p}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="p" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/81eac1e205430d1f40810df36a0edffdc367af36" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:1.259ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Conic_section#Conic_parameters" title="Conic section">semi-latus rectum</a>, while <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle e}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>e</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle e}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="e" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cd253103f0876afc68ebead27a5aa9867d927467" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.083ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Orbital_eccentricity" title="Orbital eccentricity">orbital eccentricity</a>, all obtainable from the various forms of the six independent <a href="/wiki/Orbital_elements" title="Orbital elements">orbital elements</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Circular_orbits">Circular orbits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orbital_mechanics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Circular orbits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>All bounded orbits where the gravity of a central body dominates are elliptical in nature. A special case of this is the circular orbit, which is an ellipse of zero eccentricity. The formula for the velocity of a body in a circular orbit at distance <i>r</i> from the center of gravity of mass <i>M</i> can be derived as follows -\n</p><p>Centrifugal acceleration matches the acceleration due to gravity.\n</p><p>So, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v^{2}/r=GM/r^{2}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>G</mi>\n<mi>M</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<msup>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v^{2}/r=GM/r^{2}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle v^{2}/r=GM/r^{2}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9972a81b0e942b13271bf4ca409274abc6d02d72" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:15.026ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span>\n</p><p>Therefore,\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\ v={\\sqrt {{\\frac {GM}{r}}\\ }}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>G</mi>\n<mi>M</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\ v={\\sqrt {{\\frac {GM}{r}}\\ }}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\ v = \\sqrt{\\frac{GM} {r}\\ }" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3c8baea40bef1c9ac3ba24d9f240ffd9d3835eb0" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:12.816ex; height:6.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle G}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>G</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle G}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="G" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f5f3c8921a3b352de45446a6789b104458c9f90b" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.827ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is the <a href="/wiki/Gravitational_constant" title="Gravitational constant">gravitational constant</a>, equal to\n</p>\n<dl><dd>6.673 84 &#215; 10<sup>&#8722;11</sup> m<sup>3</sup>/(kg&#183;s<sup>2</sup>)</dd></dl>\n<p>To properly use this formula, the units must be consistent; for example, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle M}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>M</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle M}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="M" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f82cade9898ced02fdd08712e5f0c0151758a0dd" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.442ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> must be in kilograms, and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle r}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0d1ecb613aa2984f0576f70f86650b7c2a132538" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.049ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> must be in meters. The answer will be in meters per second.\n</p><p>The quantity <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle GM}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>G</mi>\n<mi>M</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle GM}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="GM" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d2d9b5427dc6e6f3c11f13d88a5b637b4bc24585" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:4.269ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is often termed the <a href="/wiki/Standard_gravitational_parameter" title="Standard gravitational parameter">standard gravitational parameter</a>, which has a different value for every planet or moon in the <a href="/wiki/Solar_System" title="Solar System">Solar System</a>.\n</p><p>Once the circular orbital velocity is known, the <a href="/wiki/Escape_velocity" title="Escape velocity">escape velocity</a> is easily found by multiplying by the <a href="/wiki/Square_root_of_2" title="Square root of 2">square root of 2</a>:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\ v={\\sqrt {2}}{\\sqrt {{\\frac {GM}{r}}\\ }}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {2GM}{r}}\\ }}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mn>2</mn>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>G</mi>\n<mi>M</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>G</mi>\n<mi>M</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\ v={\\sqrt {2}}{\\sqrt {{\\frac {GM}{r}}\\ }}={\\sqrt {{\\frac {2GM}{r}}\\ }}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\ v = \\sqrt 2\\sqrt{\\frac {GM} {r}\\ } = \\sqrt{\\frac {2GM} {r}\\ }." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6ce5f6194c939b417dc6d08a36e6713f87c57321" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:28.832ex; height:6.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>To escape from gravity, the kinetic energy must at least match the negative potential energy.\nSo, <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle 1/2mv^{2}=GMm/r}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mi>G</mi>\n<mi>M</mi>\n<mi>m</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>/</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle 1/2mv^{2}=GMm/r}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle 1/2mv^{2}=GMm/r}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f6aeeebbe9c814d23f6dc6537be08b6211fe52f7" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:19.328ex; height:3.176ex;"/></span> and therefore,\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v={\\sqrt {{\\frac {2GM}{r}}\\ }}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>G</mi>\n<mi>M</mi>\n</mrow>\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mtext>&#160;</mtext>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n<mo>.</mo>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v={\\sqrt {{\\frac {2GM}{r}}\\ }}.}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle v={\\sqrt {{\\frac {2GM}{r}}\\ }}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/567486d6bd4e22d157701c6afb550228d07ba12a" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:14.045ex; height:6.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Elliptical_orbits">Elliptical orbits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orbital_mechanics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Elliptical orbits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>If <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle 0&lt;e&lt;1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mn>0</mn>\n<mo>&lt;</mo>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mo>&lt;</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle 0&lt;e&lt;1}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="0&lt;e&lt;1" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/679de8c4138507493a1cc5adc572bb0ffdd19a82" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:9.605ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, then the denominator of the equation of free orbits varies with the true anomaly <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\theta }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\theta }</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\theta " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6e5ab2664b422d53eb0c7df3b87e1360d75ad9af" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.09ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, but remains positive, never becoming zero. Therefore, the relative position vector remains bounded, having its smallest magnitude at periapsis <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle r_{p}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>p</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r_{p}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r_{p}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d02ec163fac8837ac757005d783b375e52808b97" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:2.108ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span>, which is given by:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle r_{p}={\\frac {p}{1+e}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>p</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mrow>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>e</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r_{p}={\\frac {p}{1+e}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r_p=\\frac{p}{1+e}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d327e3493f643cc37ded75593b1c62c1c2e20f6c" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:11.129ex; height:5.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>The maximum value <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle r}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0d1ecb613aa2984f0576f70f86650b7c2a132538" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.049ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is reached when <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\theta =180^{\\circ }}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msup>\n<mn>180</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mo>&#8728;<!-- &#8728; --></mo>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\theta =180^{\\circ }}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\theta =180^{\\circ }}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/acfe2a9d00d19df1cda947de4bd87632ffa66a14" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:8.731ex; height:2.343ex;"/></span>. This point is called the apoapsis, and its radial coordinate, denoted <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle r_{a}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r_{a}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r_{a}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/da5f0781a46ba20129a554237056b6ade78b956f" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.151ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span>, is\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle r_{a}={\\frac {p}{1-e}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mrow>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mi>e</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r_{a}={\\frac {p}{1-e}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r_a=\\frac{p}{1-e}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0bcdb0dbf8e315f6caff80e6258da198e97a1ea7" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:11.171ex; height:5.009ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Let <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle 2a}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle 2a}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="2a" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d325c24be7d760207674a169b078892bdd5cbc76" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:2.392ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> be the distance measured along the apse line from periapsis <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle P}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>P</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle P}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="P" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b4dc73bf40314945ff376bd363916a738548d40a" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.745ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> to apoapsis <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle A}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>A</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle A}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="A" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7daff47fa58cdfd29dc333def748ff5fa4c923e3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.743ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>, as illustrated in the equation below:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle 2a=r_{p}+r_{a}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>p</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<msub>\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle 2a=r_{p}+r_{a}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="2a=r_p+r_a" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/eae29940b03af33d9e123a2f6b12eb71a2230fb1" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:12.589ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>Substituting the equations above, we get:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle a={\\frac {p}{1-e^{2}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>p</mi>\n<mrow>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle a={\\frac {p}{1-e^{2}}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="a=\\frac{p}{1-e^2}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e5d52bffe635084653d865344f975d6e0fc642a1" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:11.305ex; height:5.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>a is the semimajor axis of the ellipse. Solving for <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle p}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>p</mi>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle p}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="p" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/81eac1e205430d1f40810df36a0edffdc367af36" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; margin-left: -0.089ex; width:1.259ex; height:2.009ex;"/></span>, and substituting the result in the conic section curve formula above, we get:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle r={\\frac {a(1-e^{2})}{1+e\\cos \\theta }}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mo stretchy="false">(</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<msup>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mo stretchy="false">)</mo>\n</mrow>\n<mrow>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mi>cos</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r={\\frac {a(1-e^{2})}{1+e\\cos \\theta }}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r=\\frac{a(1-e^2)}{1+e\\cos\\theta}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/11254ed7939c4b7ea681bc9d7af7f2de4f44f49b" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:15.045ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Orbital_period">Orbital period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orbital_mechanics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Orbital period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Under standard assumptions the <a href="/wiki/Orbital_period" title="Orbital period">orbital period</a> (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T\\,\\!}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mspace width="negativethinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T\\,\\!}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="T\\,\\!" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8e6be5af8259cedf1aac5ae3f6a5fad65ec2ef87" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; margin-right: -0.387ex; width:2.023ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span>) of a body traveling along an elliptic orbit can be computed as:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle T=2\\pi {\\sqrt {a^{3} \\over {\\mu }}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>T</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>&#960;<!-- &#960; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mfrac>\n<msup>\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>3</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle T=2\\pi {\\sqrt {a^{3} \\over {\\mu }}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="T=2\\pi\\sqrt{a^3\\over{\\mu}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/38956de3e1f0c64e63fa4444e2ef458f81e5d6f3" style="vertical-align: -3.171ex; width:12.673ex; height:7.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mu \\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mu \\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\mu \\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8d20addf0d9f04e185714134b97726c4bf17d340" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:1.789ex; height:2.176ex;"/></span> is <a href="/wiki/Standard_gravitational_parameter" title="Standard gravitational parameter">standard gravitational parameter</a>,</li>\n<li><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle a\\,\\!}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mspace width="negativethinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle a\\,\\!}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="a\\,\\!" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/99a94f96d2455b9d7faf3cec3eb02ab3c455aec1" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; margin-right: -0.387ex; width:1.617ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is length of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-major_axis" title="Semi-major axis">semi-major axis</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>Conclusions:\n</p>\n<ul><li>The orbital period is equal to that for a <a href="/wiki/Circular_orbit" title="Circular orbit">circular orbit</a> with the orbit radius equal to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-major_axis" title="Semi-major axis">semi-major axis</a> (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle a\\,\\!}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>a</mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n<mspace width="negativethinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle a\\,\\!}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="a\\,\\!" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/99a94f96d2455b9d7faf3cec3eb02ab3c455aec1" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; margin-right: -0.387ex; width:1.617ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>),</li>\n<li>For a given semi-major axis the orbital period does not depend on the eccentricity (See also: <a href="/wiki/Kepler%27s_laws_of_planetary_motion#Third_law" title="Kepler\'s laws of planetary motion">Kepler\'s third law</a>).</li></ul>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Velocity">Velocity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orbital_mechanics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Velocity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Under standard assumptions the <a href="/wiki/Orbital_speed" title="Orbital speed">orbital speed</a> (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v\\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v\\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8b67d1fd725a759a151374b793113d7a78a65da4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.515ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>) of a body traveling along an <b>elliptic orbit</b> can be computed from the <a href="/wiki/Vis-viva_equation" title="Vis-viva equation">Vis-viva equation</a> as:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v={\\sqrt {\\mu \\left({2 \\over {r}}-{1 \\over {a}}\\right)}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n<mrow>\n<mo>(</mo>\n<mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mrow>\n<mo>)</mo>\n</mrow>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v={\\sqrt {\\mu \\left({2 \\over {r}}-{1 \\over {a}}\\right)}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v=\\sqrt{\\mu\\left({2\\over{r}}-{1\\over{a}}\\right)}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b2ef876b8914830177588da15dbc9e431464da9e" style="vertical-align: -3.171ex; width:18.665ex; height:7.509ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\mu \\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mu \\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\mu \\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8d20addf0d9f04e185714134b97726c4bf17d340" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; margin-right: -0.387ex; width:1.617ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is the length of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Semi-major_axis" title="Semi-major axis">semi-major axis</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>The velocity equation for a <a href="/wiki/Hyperbolic_trajectory" title="Hyperbolic trajectory">hyperbolic trajectory</a> has either + <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {1 \\over {a}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>a</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle {1 \\over {a}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{1\\over{a}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c318d7de3d62af8a6add28f57c3914aace20c583" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:2.066ex; height:5.176ex;"/></span>, or it is the same with the convention that in that case <i>a</i> is negative.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orbital_mechanics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Under standard assumptions, <a href="/wiki/Specific_orbital_energy" title="Specific orbital energy">specific orbital energy</a> (<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\epsilon \\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; width:1.331ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>) of elliptic orbit is negative and the orbital energy conservation equation (the <a href="/wiki/Vis-viva_equation" title="Vis-viva equation">Vis-viva equation</a>) for this orbit can take the form:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle {v^{2} \\over {2}}-{\\mu  \\over {r}}=-{\\mu  \\over {2a}}=\\epsilon &lt;0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<msup>\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</msup>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>2</mn>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>&#8722;<!-- &#8722; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mn>1</mn>\n<mo>+</mo>\n<mi>cos</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; --></mo>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r={{h^{2}} \\over {\\mu }}{{1} \\over {1+\\cos \\theta }}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r={{h^2}\\over{\\mu}}{{1}\\over{1+\\cos\\theta}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1e736d64e322f919e0accce5c07944b041ce14e0" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:16.804ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle r\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>r</mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle r\\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="r\\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f08ce4d4c86c5b43f36c8435fb598da6471047c6" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.436ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is the radial distance of the orbiting body from the mass center of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_body" title="Central body">central body</a>,</li>\n<li><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle h\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>h</mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle h\\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="h\\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/cecd947e6666832fcc39909b00dbde70caa9cf8c" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; --></mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\mu \\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\mu \\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8d20addf0d9f04e185714134b97726c4bf17d340" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; approaches 180&#176;, the denominator approaches zero, so that <i>r</i> tends towards infinity. Hence, the energy of the trajectory for which <i>e</i>=1 is zero, and is given by:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\epsilon ={v^{2} \\over 2}-{\\mu  \\over {r}}=0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>&#1013;<!-- &#1013; --></mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mfrac>\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</mrow>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mn>0</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\epsilon ={v^{2} \\over 2}-{\\mu  \\over {r}}=0}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="\\epsilon={v^2\\over2}-{\\mu\\over{r}}=0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/82a0b65e3fcb6a9b7d3441c35f21d10b21302dbb" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:16.4ex; height:5.676ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>where:\n</p>\n<ul><li><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v\\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mspace width="thinmathspace"></mspace>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v\\,}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v\\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8b67d1fd725a759a151374b793113d7a78a65da4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.515ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span> is the speed of the orbiting body.</li></ul>\n<p>In other words, the speed anywhere on a parabolic path is:\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle v={\\sqrt {2\\mu  \\over {r}}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>v</mi>\n<mo>=</mo>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<msqrt>\n<mfrac>\n<mrow>\n<mn>2</mn>\n<mi>&#956;<!-- &#956; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi>r</mi>\n</mrow>\n</mfrac>\n</msqrt>\n</mrow>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle v={\\sqrt {2\\mu  \\over {r}}}}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="v=\\sqrt{2\\mu\\over{r}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/dcaa895efed097dd9e420d787bc17327814b0c24" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:9.95ex; height:6.343ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hyperbolic_orbits">Hyperbolic orbits</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Orbital_mechanics&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Hyperbolic orbits">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>If <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle e&gt;1}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>e</mi>\n<mo>&gt;</mo>\n<mn>1</mn>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle e&gt;1}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="e&gt;1" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9605ca17e3915b659685c0326fbbcbfb522f11b3" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:18.275ex; height:6.176ex;"/></span></dd></dl>\n<p>describes the geometry of the hyperbolic orbit. The system consists of two symmetric curves. The orbiting body occupies one of them; the other one is its empty mathematical image. Clearly, the denominator of the equation above goes to zero when <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\cos \\theta =-1/e}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<mi>cos</mi>\n<mo>&#8289;<!-- &#8289; width:12.904ex; height:2.843ex;"/></span>. we denote this value of true anomaly\n</p>\n<dl><dd><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\theta _{\\infty }=\\cos ^{-1}\\left(-{\\frac {1}{e}}\\right)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; Observe that <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math alttext="{\\displaystyle \\theta _{\\infty }}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n<semantics>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n<msub>\n<mi>&#952;<!-- &#952; --></mi>\n<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n<mi mathvariant="normal">&#8734;<!-- &#8734; --></mi>\n</mrow>\n</msub>\n</mstyle>\n</mrow>\n<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\\displaystyle \\theta _{\\infty }}</annotation>\n</semantics>\n</math></span><img alt="{\\displaystyle \\theta _{\\infty }}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c76cc505c3f70455ad22fe805b5246824425bab2" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:2.966ex; height:2.509ex;"/></span> lies between 90&#176; and 180&#176;.
